At application startup, passes are registered\n// with the PassRegistry, which is later provided to the PassManager for\n// dependency resolution and similar tasks.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_PASSREGISTRY_H\n#define LLVM_PASSREGISTRY_H\n\n#include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/StringMap.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/RWMutex.h\"\n#include <memory>\n#include <vector>\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\nclass PassInfo;\nstruct PassRegistrationListener;\n\n/// PassRegistry - This class manages the registration and intitialization of\n/// the pass subsystem as application startup, and assists the PassManager\n/// in resolving pass dependencies.\n/// NOTE: PassRegistry is NOT thread-safe.  If you want to use LLVM on multiple\n/// threads simultaneously, you will need to use a separate PassRegistry on\n/// each thread.\nclass PassRegistry {\n  mutable sys::SmartRWMutex<true> Lock;\n\n  /// PassInfoMap - Keep track of the PassInfo object for each registered pass.\n  using MapType = DenseMap<const void *, const PassInfo *>;\n  MapType PassInfoMap;\n\n  using StringMapType = StringMap<const PassInfo *>;\n  StringMapType PassInfoStringMap;\n\n  std::vector<std::unique_ptr<const PassInfo>> ToFree;\n  std::vector<PassRegistrationListener *> Listeners;\n\npublic:\n  PassRegistry() = default;\n  LLVM_ABI ~PassRegistry();\n\n  /// getPassRegistry - Access the global registry object, which is\n  /// automatically initialized at application launch and destroyed by\n  /// llvm_shutdown.\n  LLVM_ABI static PassRegistry *getPassRegistry();\n\n  /// getPassInfo - Look up a pass' corresponding PassInfo, indexed by the pass'\n  /// type identifier (&MyPass::ID).\n  LLVM_ABI const PassInfo *getPassInfo(const void *TI) const;\n\n  /// getPassInfo - Look up a pass' corresponding PassInfo, indexed by the pass'\n  /// argument string.\n  LLVM_ABI const PassInfo *getPassInfo(StringRef Arg) const;\n\n  /// registerPass - Register a pass (by means of its PassInfo) with the\n  /// registry.  Required in order to use the pass with a PassManager.\n  LLVM_ABI void registerPass(const PassInfo &PI, bool ShouldFree = false);\n\n  /// enumerateWith - Enumerate the registered passes, calling the provided\n  /// PassRegistrationListener's passEnumerate() callback on each of them.\n  LLVM_ABI void enumerateWith(PassRegistrationListener *L);\n\n  /// addRegistrationListener - Register the given PassRegistrationListener\n  /// to receive passRegistered() callbacks whenever a new pass is registered.\n  LLVM_ABI void addRegistrationListener(PassRegistrationListener *L);\n\n  /// removeRegistrationListener - Unregister a PassRegistrationListener so that\n  /// it no longer receives passRegistered() callbacks.\n  LLVM_ABI void removeRegistrationListener(PassRegistrationListener *L);\n};\n\n} // end namespace llvm\n\n#endif // LLVM_PASSREGISTRY_H\n","numLines":88,"startLine":1,"totalLines":88}}}

There\n    11→/// is no \"pass\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\n    12→/// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\n    13→/// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\n    14→/// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\n    15→/// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\n    16→/// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\n    17→/// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\n    18→/// single There\n/// is no \"pass\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\n/// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\n/// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\n/// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\n/// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\n/// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\n/// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\n/// single module provided.\n///\n/// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\n/// modules and functions.\n///\n/// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\n///   a Function.\n/// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\n///\n/// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\n/// polymorphism as outlined in the \"Value Semantics and Concept-based\n/// Polymorphism\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \"Inheritance Is The Base\n/// Class of Evil\") by Sean Parent:\n/// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\n/// * http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_BpMYeUFXv8\n/// * https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/shows/goingnative-2013/inheritance-base-class-of-evil\n///\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\n#define LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\n\n#include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/STLExtras.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/StringExtras.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/TinyPtrVector.h\"\n#include \"llvm/IR/Analysis.h\"\n#include \"llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/TypeName.h\"\n#include <cassert>\n#include <cstring>\n#include <list>\n#include <memory>\n#include <tuple>\n#include <type_traits>\n#include <utility>\n#include <vector>\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\nclass Function;\nclass Module;\n\n// Forward declare the analysis manager template.\ntemplate <typename IRUnitT, typename... ExtraArgTs> class AnalysisManager;\n\n/// A CRTP mix-in to automatically provide informational APIs needed for\n/// passes.\n///\n/// This provides some boilerplate for types that are passes.\ntemplate <typename DerivedT> struct PassInfoMixin {\n  /// Gets the name of the pass we are mixed into.\n  static StringRef name() {\n    static_assert(std::is_base_of<PassInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\n                  \"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\");\n    StringRef Name = getTypeName<DerivedT>();\n    Name.consume_front(\"llvm::\");\n    return Name;\n  }\n\n  void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\n                     function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\n    StringRef ClassName = DerivedT::name();\n    auto PassName = MapClassName2PassName(ClassName);\n    OS << PassName;\n  }\n};\n\n/// A CRTP mix-in that provides informational APIs needed for analysis passes.\n///\n/// This provides some boilerplate for types that are analysis passes. As a special shortcut, if the very first pass is not\n  /// a module pass (as a module pass manager is), this will automatically form\n  /// the shortest stack of pass managers that allow inserting that first pass.\n  /// So, assuming function passes 'fpassN', CGSCC passes 'cgpassN', and loop\n  /// passes 'lpassN', all of these are valid:\n  ///\n  ///   fpass1,fpass2,fpass3\n  ///   cgpass1,cgpass2,cgpass3\n  ///   lpass1,lpass2,lpass3\n  ///\n  /// And they are equivalent to the following (resp.):\n  ///\n  ///   module(function(fpass1,fpass2,fpass3))\n  ///   module(cgscc(cgpass1,cgpass2,cgpass3))\n  ///   module(function(loop(lpass1,lpass2,lpass3)))\n  ///\n  /// This shortcut is especially useful for debugging and testing small pass\n  /// combinations.\n  ///\n  /// The sequence of passes aren't necessarily the exact same kind of pass.\n  /// You can mix different levels implicitly if adaptor passes are defined to\n  /// make them work. For example,\n  ///\n  ///   mpass1,fpass1,fpass2,mpass2,lpass1\n  ///\n  /// This pipeline uses only one pass manager: the top-level module manager.\n  /// fpass1,fpass2 and lpass1 are added into the top-level module manager\n  /// using only adaptor passes. No nested function/loop pass managers are\n  /// added. The purpose is to allow easy pass testing when the user\n  /// specifically want the pass to run under a adaptor directly. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01SNJ9qtkmq1XWkYSNTm6LVu","type":"tool_result","content":"  // Distribute loops to allow partial vectorization.  I.e. isolate dependences\n  // into separate loop that would otherwise inhibit vectorization. As a result,\n  // LoopSink pass needs to be a very late IR pass to avoid undoing LICM\n  // result too early.\n  OptimizePM.addPass(LoopSinkPass());\n\n  // And finally clean up LCSSA form before generating code.\n  OptimizePM.addPass(InstSimplifyPass());\n\n  // This hoists/decomposes div/rem ops. Clean up the CFG.\n  OptimizePM.addPass(\n      SimplifyCFGPass(SimplifyCFGOptions()\n                          .convertSwitchRangeToICmp(true)\n                          .convertSwitchToArithmetic(true)\n                          .speculateUnpredictables(true)\n                          .hoistLoadsStoresWithCondFaulting(true)));\n\n  // Add the core optimizing pipeline.\n  MPM.addPass(createModuleToFunctionPassAdaptor(std::move(OptimizePM),\n                                                PTO.EagerlyInvalidateAnalyses));\n\n  // AllocToken transforms heap allocation calls; this needs to run late after\n  // other allocation call transformations (such as those in InstCombine).\n  if (!LTOPreLink)\n    MPM.addPass(AllocTokenPass());\n\n  invokeOptimizerLastEPCallbacks(MPM, Level, LTOPhase);\n\n  // Split out cold code. Splitting is done late to avoid hiding context from\n  // other optimizations and inadvertently regressing performance. If enough similar regions can\n  // be found where extracting the regions into their own function will decrease\n  // the size of the program, we extract the regions, a deduplicate the\n  // structurally similar regions.\n  if (EnableIROutliner)\n    MPM.addPass(IROutlinerPass());\n\n  // Now we need to do some global optimization transforms.\n  // FIXME: It would seem like these should come first in the optimization\n  // pipeline and maybe be the bottom of the canonicalization pipeline? It has a better chance to merge functions\n  // after ConstantMerge folded jump tables.\n  if (PTO.MergeFunctions)\n    MPM.addPass(MergeFunctionsPass());\n\n  if (PTO.CallGraphProfile && !LTOPreLink)\n    MPM.addPass(CGProfilePass(isLTOPostLink(LTOPhase)));\n\n  // RelLookupTableConverterPass runs later in LTO post-link pipeline.\n  if (!LTOPreLink)\n    MPM.addPass(RelLookupTableConverterPass());\n\n  // Add devirtualization pass only when LTO is not enabled, as otherwise\n  // the pass is already enabled in the LTO pipeline.\n  if (PTO.DevirtualizeSpeculatively && LTOPhase == ThinOrFullLTOPhase::None) {\n    // TODO: explore a better pipeline configuration that can improve\n    // compilation time overhead.\n    MPM.addPass(WholeProgramDevirtPass(\n        /*ExportSummary*/ nullptr,\n        /*ImportSummary*/ nullptr,\n        /*DevirtSpeculatively*/ PTO.DevirtualizeSpeculatively));\n    MPM.addPass(LowerTypeTestsPass(nullptr, nullptr,\n                                   lowertypetests::DropTestKind::Assume));\n    // Given that the devirtualization creates more opportunities for inlining,\n    // we run the Inliner again here to maximize the optimization gain we\n    // get from devirtualization.\n    // Also, we can't run devirtualization before inlining because the\n    // devirtualization depends on the passes optimizing/eliminating vtable GVs\n    // and those passes are only effective after inlining.\n    if (EnableModuleInliner) {\n      MPM.addPass(ModuleInlinerPass(getInlineParamsFromOptLevel(Level),\n                                    UseInlineAdvisor,\n                                    ThinOrFullLTOPhase::None));\n    } else {\n      MPM.addPass(ModuleInlinerWrapperPass(\n          getInlineParamsFromOptLevel(Level),\n          /* MandatoryFirst */ true,\n          InlineContext{ThinOrFullLTOPhase::None, InlinePass::CGSCCInliner}));\n    }\n  }\n  return MPM;\n}\n\nModulePassManager\nPassBuilder::buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline(OptimizationLevel Level,\n complementary mechanisms: the legacy pass manager (deprecated) and the new pass manager. Both are rooted in a centralized PassRegistry that tracks all available passes.\\n\\n## 1. PassManager Template System (New PM)\\n\\nThe core PassManager template is defined in `llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h` (lines 159-226). This is a template class parameterized by the IR unit it operates on (Module, Function, Loop, etc.). The PassManager template:\\n- Stores a vector of passes (line 225) as `std::vector<std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes`\\n- Implements the `addPass()` method (lines 193-214) which stores passes using type erasure via PassModel\\n- Contains a `run()` method that sequentially executes all contained passes\\n- Two type aliases provided: `ModulePassManager` (line 238) and `FunctionPassManager` (line 247)\\n\\n## 2. PassRegistry System (Static Registration)\\n\\nThe PassRegistry is defined in `llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h` and implemented in `llvm/lib/IR/PassRegistry.cpp`. This is a singleton that maintains two maps:\\n- `PassInfoMap`: Maps pass type identifiers (&PassClass::ID) to PassInfo objects\\n- `PassInfoStringMap`: Maps command-line argument strings to PassInfo objects\\n\\nThe `registerPass()` method (PassRegistry.cpp:48-62) inserts pass metadata and notifies registration listeners.\\n\\n## 3. Pass Registration Macros (Legacy PM)\\n\\nThe legacy pass registration mechanism uses macros defined in `llvm/include/llvm/PassSupport.h`:\\n- `INITIALIZE_PASS` (lines 56-58): Expands to create registration code\\n- `INITIALIZE_PASS_BEGIN/END` (lines 39-54): Creates a function that constructs PassInfo and calls `registry.registerPass()`\\n- These macros generate static initialization functions that execute at program startup\\n- `RegisterPass<T>` template (lines 89-98): Allows direct pass registration via global constructor\\n\\n## 4. O2/O3 Pipeline Execution Order\\n\\nThe O2/O3 optimization pipeline is constructed in `llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilderPipelines.cpp` by the `buildModuleOptimizationPipeline()` function (starting at line 1478). The execution order includes:\\n\\n### Module-Level Passes (lines 1478-1660):\\n1. `PartialInlinerPass()` - Partially inline large functions\\n2. `EliminateAvailableExternallyPass()` - Remove available external functions\\n3. `ReversePostOrderFunctionAttrsPass()` - Infer function attributes\\n4. PGO instrumentation passes (if enabled)\\n5. `RecomputeGlobalsAAPass()` - Recompute alias analysis\\n\\n### Function-Level Optimization Pipeline (lines 1660-1700):\\nUsing FunctionPassManager that adds:\\n1. `DropUnnecessaryAssumesPass()`\\n2. `LoopVersioningLICMPass()` and `LICMPass()` (if enabled)\\n3. `Float2IntPass()`\\n4. `LowerConstantIntrinsicsPass()`\\n5. `LowerMatrixIntrinsicsPass()` (if enabled)\\n6. `ControlHeightReductionPass()` (O3 only)\\n\\n### Loop Optimization Pipeline (lines 1700-1750):\\nUsing LoopPassManager:\\n1. `LoopRotatePass()`\\n2. `LoopDeletionPass()`\\n3. `LoopInterchangePass()` (if enabled)\\n4. Static Pass Registry\\n\\nAll passes are catalogued in `llvm/lib/Passes/PassRegistry.def`, which defines:\\n- MODULE_ANALYSIS: Module-level analysis passes\\n- MODULE_PASS: Module-level transformation passes\\n- CGSCC_ANALYSIS/CGSCC_PASS: Call graph SCC passes\\n- FUNCTION_ANALYSIS/FUNCTION_PASS: Function-level passes\\n- LOOP_ANALYSIS/LOOP_PASS: Loop-level passes\\n\\nThis file is included by PassBuilder to generate the pass registration and parsing infrastructure.\\n\\n## 8. Execution Flow\\n\\n1. **Initialization**: At startup, all passes call their INITIALIZE_PASS functions, registering themselves in PassRegistry\\n2. **Pipeline Selection**: Frontend calls PassBuilder::buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline() with optimization level\\n3. **Pipeline Construction**: PassBuilder methods construct nested PassManager objects, calling addPass() to add passes\\n4. **Pipeline Execution**: ModulePassManager::run() is called with the module and AnalysisManager\\n5. **Pass Execution**: Each pass is run sequentially via its operator()(Module&, ModuleAnalysisManager&)\\n6. **Analysis Invalidation**: After each pass, the AnalysisManager invalidates analyses based on PreservedAnalyses\\n\\n## Key Integration Points\\n\\n- **PassManager Template** (`llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h`): Core template-based execution engine\\n- **PassRegistry** (`llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h/cpp`): Central pass metadata repository\\n- **PassBuilder** (`llvm/include/llvm/Passes/PassBuilder.h`): High-level pipeline construction API\\n- **PassBuilderPipelines.cpp** (`llvm/lib/Passes/PassBuilderPipelines.cpp`): Implementation of optimization pipelines\\n- **PassSupport.h** (`llvm/include/llvm/PassSupport.h`): Macros for pass registration\\n- **PassRegistry.def** (`llvm/lib/Passes/PassRegistry.def`): Static declaration of all built-in passes\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":719,"cache_read_input_tokens":59276,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":719},"output_tokens":6,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a94daec2-cd69-4453-954c-a8757b48a1a1","uuid":"a9175f8a-1109-4e23-bfd7-d08b54e66429"}
